class="text-sm font-semibold">Compliance</h5></a></li></ul></div><div class="border-y border-v-border mt-4 md:mt-auto md:border-b-0 py-2 px-2"><a class="py-2 px-3 flex gap-x-2 items-center rounded cursor-pointer w-full outline-none t-body-3-semibold hover:bg-v-bg-active focus:bg-v-bg-active" href="/docs/changelog"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" fill="none" viewBox="0 0 16 16"><path fill="currentColor" d="M2.473 10.86a.7.7 0 0 0-.22-.14.67.67 0 0 0-.507 0 .7.7 0 0 0-.22.14.7.7 0 0 0-.14.22.67.67 0 0 0 .14.727q.099.089.22.14a.63.63 0 0 0 .507 0 .8.8 0 0 0 .506q.05.123.14.22.097.09.22.14a.63.63 0 0 0 .506 0 .8.8 0 0 0 .22-.14.8.8 0 0 0 .14-.22.63.63 0 0 0 0-.506.7.7 0 0 0-.14-.22M14 7.333H4.667a.667.667 0 0 0 0 1.334H14a.667.667 0 1 0 0-1.334M2.473 bg-v-bg-button text-v-text-button border-transparent hover:border-v-border-button-hover inline-flex items-center"><div class="flex gap-2 items-center justify-center"><div>Start building</div></div></a><a class="text-button text-center py-1" href="https://ui.tinybird.co/login">Sign In</a></div></div></div></nav></aside><main class="w-full grow pt-6 pb-6 md:pt-8 sm:pb-8 md:max-w-[calc(100%_-var(--sidebar-width))]" data-pagefind-body=""><div class="hidden sm:block relative max-w-7xl mx-auto px-5 md:px-6 "><nav aria-label="Breadcrumb" class="py-4 max-w-4xl md:px-4 mb-2"><ol class="flex items-center text-sm"><li><a class="hover:font-semibold hover:underline hover:text-black" href="/docs/forward/get-started/quickstarts">Home</a></li><li class="flex items-center"><span class="mx-2 text-v-text-3">/</span><a class="hover:font-semibold hover:underline hover:text-black" href="/docs/forward/work-with-data">Work with data</a></li><li class="flex items-center"><span class="mx-2 text-v-text-3">/</span><a class="hover:font-semibold hover:underline hover:text-black" href="/docs/forward/work-with-data/optimize">Optimize</a></li><li class="flex items-center"><span class="mx-2 text-v-text-3">/</span><a class="hover:font-semibold hover:underline hover:text-black" href="/docs/forward/work-with-data/optimize/guides">Guides</a></li><li class="flex items-center"><span class="mx-2 text-v-text-3">/</span><span class="font-semibold">Deduplication strategies</span></li></ol></nav></div><div class="relative max-w-7xl mx-auto px-5 md:px-6 xl:grid xl:grid-cols-[1fr_280px]"><div class="max-w-4xl text-body md:px-4 md:pb-20 relative" role="main"><article><div class="flex flex-col sm:flex-row sm:items-center justify-between gap-4 mb-6"><h1 id="deduplicate-data-in-your-data-source" class="t-h3" data-pagefind-weight="20.0">Deduplicate data in your data source<a class="headerlink" href="#deduplicate-data-in-your-data-source" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h1><div class="flex-shrink-0 w-auto"><div class="relative inline-block w-auto" data-pagefind-ignore="true"><div class="flex rounded-md overflow-hidden border border-v-border-02 hover:border-v-border-03 transition-colors"><button class="flex items-center gap-1.5 px-3 py-1.5 text-sm transition-colors min-w-[106px] text-v-text-01"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" stroke-width="2" viewBox="0 0 24 24" class="w-4 h-4 dark:invert-[0.85] dark:brightness-[0.9]"><path d="M14 2H6a2 2 0 0 0-2 2v16a2 2 0 0 0 2 2h12a2 2 0 0 0 2-2V8z"></path><path d="M14 2v6h6M16 13H8M16 17H8M10 9H8"></path></svg><span>Copy as MD</span></button><button class="flex items-center justify-center px-2 py-1.5 text-sm text-v-text-01 border-l border-v-border-02 min-w-[32px]" aria-haspopup="true" aria-expanded="false"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" fill="none" class="w-3 h-3 dark:invert-[0.85] dark:brightness-[0.9]" style="margin-top:-4px;margin-left:-4px"><path fill="currentColor" d="M8.1 11.41 4 6.995 4.745 6 8.1 9.795 11.454 6l.746.994z"></path></svg></button></div></div></div></div><p>Sometimes you might need to deduplicate data, for example to receive updates or data from a transactional database through CDC. You might want to retrieve only the latest data point, or keep a historic record of the evolution of the attributes of an object over time.<!-- --> <!-- -->Because Tinybird doesn&#x27;t enforce uniqueness for primary keys when inserting rows, you need to follow different strategies to deduplicate data with minimal side effects.</p><h2 id="deduplication-strategies" class="t-h4 font-semibold mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="12.0">Deduplication strategies<a class="headerlink" href="#deduplication-strategies" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h2><p>You can use one of the following strategies to deduplicate your data.</p><div class="max-w-[calc(100%_+_40px)] overflow-auto -mx-5 ps-5 md:max-w-full md:mx-0 md:ps-0"><table><thead><tr><th>Method</th><th>When to use</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td><a href="#deduplicate-at-query-time">Deduplicate at query time</a></td><td>Deduplicate data at query time if you are still prototyping or the data source is small.</td></tr><tr><td><a href="#use-the-replacingmergetree-engine">Use ReplacingMergeTree</a></td><td>Use <code>ReplacingMergeTree</code> or <code>AggregatingMergeTree</code> for greater performance.</td></tr><tr><td><a href="#snapshot-based-deduplication">Snapshot based deduplication</a></td><td>If data freshness isn&#x27;t required, generate periodic snapshots of the data and take advantage of subsequent materialized views for rollups.</td></tr><tr><td><a href="#hybrid-approach-using-lambda-architecture">Hybrid approach using Lambda architecture</a></td><td>When you need to overcome engine approach limitations while preserving freshness, combine approaches in a Lambda architecture.</td></tr><tr><td>Using argMax with null values</td><td></td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class="my-4 flex items-start gap-2 py-3 px-4 rounded border border-v-border bg-v-callout-tip text-brand-dark"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" fill="none" viewBox="0 0 16 16" class="inline shrink-0 mt-px h-5"><path fill="currentColor" d="M11.393 1.88A5.33 5.33 0 0 0 6.94.773a5.33 5.33 0 0 0-4.18 4.214A5.38 5.38 0 0 0 3.907 9.42c.469.53.738 1.206.76 1.913v2a2 2 0 0 0 2 2h2.666a2 2 0 0 0 2-2V11.46c.023-.78.31-1.53.814-2.127a5.334 5.334 0 0 0-.754-7.466zM10 13.333a.667.667 0 0 1-.667.667H6.667A.667.667 0 0 1 6 13.333v-.666h4zm1.113-4.826A4.75 4.75 0 0 0 10 11.333H8.667v-2a.667.667 0 0 0-1.334 0v2H6A4.33 4.33 0 0 0 4.933 8.56a4 4 0 0 1 4.02-6.447A4 4 0 0 1 12 6c.005.913-.309 1.8-.887 2.507"></path></svg><div class="text-v-text"><p>For dimensional and small tables, a periodical full replace is usually the best option.</p></div></div><h2 id="example-case" class="t-h4 font-semibold mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="12.0">Example case<a class="headerlink" href="#example-case" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h2><p>Consider a dataset from a social media analytics company that wants to track some data content over time. You receive an event with the latest info for each post, identified by <code>post_id</code>. The three fields, <code>views</code>, <code>likes</code>, <code>tags</code>, vary from event to event. For example:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-header"><div class="snippet-headerInfo overflow"><h5 class="snippet-title as-font--caption-bold as-cap overflow mr-4" title="post.ndjson">post.ndjson</h5></div></div><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">{ &quot;timestamp&quot;: &quot;2024-07-02T02:22:17&quot;, &quot;post_id&quot;: 956, &quot;views&quot;: 856875, &quot;likes&quot;: 2321, &quot;tags&quot;: &quot;Sports&quot; }
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><h2 id="deduplicate-at-query-time" class="t-h4 font-semibold mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="12.0">Deduplicate at query time<a class="headerlink" href="#deduplicate-at-query-time" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h2><p>Imagine you&#x27;re only interested in the latest value of views for each post. In that case, you can deduplicate data on <code>post_id</code> and get the latest value with these strategies:</p><ul><li><p>Get the max date for each post in a subquery and then filter by its results.</p></li><li><p>Group data by <code>post_id</code> and use the <code>argMax</code> function.</p></li><li><p>Use the <code>LIMIT BY</code> clause.</p></li></ul><p>Select <code>Subquery</code>, <code>argMax</code>, or <code>LIMIT BY</code> to see the example queries for each.</p><div class="w-full"><div class="bg-bg-darkest rounded-t-md overflow-hidden"><ul role="tablist" class="relative flex justify-start list-none ps-0 before:h-2 before:bg-bg-darkest before:w-full before:absolute before:-bottom-1 before:-z-[1]"><li class="m-0 w-auto"><button role="tab" aria-selected="true" class="py-3 px-4 text-caption text-white transition-all bg-bg-dark font-bold">Subquery</button></li><li class="m-0 w-auto"><button role="tab" aria-selected="false" class="py-3 px-4 text-caption text-white transition-all opacity-60 hover:opacity-100 hover:underline hover:font-bold">argMax</button></li><li class="m-0 w-auto"><button role="tab" aria-selected="false" class="py-3 px-4 text-caption text-white transition-all opacity-60 hover:opacity-100 hover:underline hover:font-bold">LIMIT BY</button></li></ul></div><div class="code-tab-content [&amp;_.snippet]:rounded-t-none"><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-header"><div class="snippet-headerInfo overflow"><h5 class="snippet-title as-font--caption-bold as-cap overflow mr-4" title="Deduplicating data on post_id using Subquery">Deduplicating data on post_id using Subquery</h5></div></div><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">SELECT *
FROM posts_info
WHERE (post_id, timestamp) IN
(
    SELECT
        post_id,
        max(timestamp)
    FROM posts_info
    GROUP BY post_id
)
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div></div></div><p>Depending on your data and how you define the sorting keys in your data sources to store it on disk, one approach is faster than the others.</p><p>In general, deduplicating at query time is fine if the size of your data is small. If you have lots of data, use a specific Engine that takes care of deduplication for you.</p><h2 id="use-the-replacingmergetree-engine" class="t-h4 font-semibold mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="12.0">Use the ReplacingMergeTree engine<a class="headerlink" href="#use-the-replacingmergetree-engine" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h2><p>If you&#x27;ve lots of data and you&#x27;re interested in the latest insertion for each unique key, use the <a href="/docs/sql-reference/engines/replacingmergetree">ReplacingMergeTree</a> engine with the following options: <code>ENGINE_SORTING_KEY</code>, <code>ENGINE_VER</code>, and <code>ENGINE_IS_DELETED</code>.</p><ul><li><p>Rows with the same <code>ENGINE_SORTING_KEY</code> are deduplicated. You can select one or more columns.</p></li><li><p>If you specify a type for <code>ENGINE_VER</code>, the row with the highest <code>ENGINE_VER</code> for each unique <code>ENGINE_SORTING_KEY</code> is kept, for example a timestamp.</p></li><li><p><code>ENGINE_IS_DELETED</code> is only active if you use <code>ENGINE_VER</code>. This column determines whether the row represents the state or is to be deleted; <code>1</code> is a deleted row, <code>0</code> is a state row. The type must be <code>UInt8</code>.</p></li><li><p>You can omit <code>ENGINE_VER</code>, so that the last inserted row for each unique <code>ENGINE_SORTING_KEY</code> is kept.</p></li></ul><div class="my-4 flex items-start gap-2 py-3 px-4 rounded border border-v-border bg-v-callout-caution text-[#856100]"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" fill="none" viewBox="0 0 16 16" class="inline shrink-0 mt-px h-5"><path fill="currentColor" d="M8.333 10.216a.666.666 0 1 0 0 1.332.666.666 0 0 0 0-1.332m7.114.98L10.08 1.862a2 2 0 0 0-3.493 0l-5.334 9.334a2 2 0 0 0 1.707 3.02h10.747a2 2 0 0 0 1.74-3.02m-1.154 1.333a.67.67 0 0 1-.586.34H2.96a.67.67 0 0 1-.587-.34.67.67 0 0 1 0-.667L7.707 2.53a.667.667 0 0 1 1.186 0l5.367 9.333a.67.67 0 0 1 .033.68zm-5.96-7.647a.667.667 0 0 0-.666.667v2.667a.667.667 0 1 0 1.333 0V5.549a.667.667 0 0 0-.667-.667"></path></svg><div class="text-v-text"><p>Do not build materialized views with an AggregatingMergeTree on top of a ReplacingMergeTree. The target data source will always contain duplicates due to the incremental nature of materialized views.</p></div></div><h3 id="define-a-data-source" class="t-body-1 font-medium mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="8.0">Define a data source<a class="headerlink" href="#define-a-data-source" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h3><p>Define a data source like the following:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-header"><div class="snippet-headerInfo overflow"><h5 class="snippet-title as-font--caption-bold as-cap overflow mr-4" title="post_views_rmt.datasource">post_views_rmt.datasource</h5></div></div><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">DESCRIPTION &gt;
    data source to save post info. ReplacingMergeTree Engine.

SCHEMA &gt;
    `post_id` Int32 `json:$.post_id`,
    `views` Int32 `json:$.views`,
    `likes` Int32 `json:$.likes`,
    `tag` String `json:$.tag`,
    `timestamp` DateTime `json:$.timestamp`,
    `_is_deleted` UInt8 `json:$._is_deleted`

ENGINE &quot;ReplacingMergeTree&quot;
ENGINE_PARTITION_KEY &quot;&quot;
ENGINE_SORTING_KEY &quot;post_id&quot;
ENGINE_VER &quot;timestamp&quot;
ENGINE_IS_DELETED &quot;_is_deleted&quot;
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><p>ReplacingMergeTree deduplicates during a merge, and merges can&#x27;t be controlled. Consider adding the <code>FINAL</code> clause, or an alternative deduplication method, to apply the merge at query time. Note also that rows are masked, not removed, when using <code>FINAL</code>.</p><div class="w-full"><div class="bg-bg-darkest rounded-t-md overflow-hidden"><ul role="tablist" class="relative flex justify-start list-none ps-0 before:h-2 before:bg-bg-darkest before:w-full before:absolute before:-bottom-1 before:-z-[1]"><li class="m-0 w-auto"><button role="tab" aria-selected="true" class="py-3 px-4 text-caption text-white transition-all bg-bg-dark font-bold">FINAL</button></li><li class="m-0 w-auto"><button role="tab" aria-selected="false" class="py-3 px-4 text-caption text-white transition-all opacity-60 hover:opacity-100 hover:underline hover:font-bold">Subquery</button></li><li class="m-0 w-auto"><button role="tab" aria-selected="false" class="py-3 px-4 text-caption text-white transition-all opacity-60 hover:opacity-100 hover:underline hover:font-bold">argMax</button></li><li class="m-0 w-auto"><button role="tab" aria-selected="false" class="py-3 px-4 text-caption text-white transition-all opacity-60 hover:opacity-100 hover:underline hover:font-bold">LIMIT BY</button></li></ul></div><div class="code-tab-content [&amp;_.snippet]:rounded-t-none"><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-header"><div class="snippet-headerInfo overflow"><h5 class="snippet-title as-font--caption-bold as-cap overflow mr-4" title="Deduplicating data on post_id using FINAL">Deduplicating data on post_id using FINAL</h5></div></div><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">SELECT *
FROM posts_info_rmt FINAL
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div></div></div><p>You can define the <code>posts_info_rmt</code> as the landing data source, the one you send events to, or as a materialized view from <code>posts_info</code>. You can also create a data source with an <code>AggregatingMergeTree</code> Engine using <code>maxState(ts)</code> and <code>argMaxState(field,ts)</code>.</p><h2 id="snapshot-based-deduplication" class="t-h4 font-semibold mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="12.0">Snapshot based deduplication<a class="headerlink" href="#snapshot-based-deduplication" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h2><p>Use <a href="/docs/forward/work-with-data/optimize/copy-pipes">Copy Pipes</a> to take a query result and write it to a new data source in the following situations:</p><ul><li>You need other Sorting Keys that might change with updates.</li><li>You need to do rollups and want to use materialized views.</li><li>Response times are too long with a <code>ReplacingMergeTree</code>.</li></ul><p>The following is an example snapshot:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-header"><div class="snippet-headerInfo overflow"><h5 class="snippet-title as-font--caption-bold as-cap overflow mr-4" title="post_generate_snapshot.pipe">post_generate_snapshot.pipe</h5></div></div><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">NODE gen_snapshot
SQL &gt;

    SELECT
        post_id,
        argMax(views, timestamp) views,
        argMax(likes, timestamp) likes,
        argMax(tag, timestamp) tag,
        max(timestamp) as ts,
        toStartOfMinute(now()) - INTERVAL 1 MINUTE as snapshot_ts
    FROM posts_info
    WHERE timestamp &lt;= toStartOfMinute(now()) - INTERVAL 1 MINUTE
    GROUP BY post_id

TYPE COPY
TARGET_DATASOURCE post_snapshot
COPY_MODE replace
COPY_SCHEDULE 0 * * * *
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><p>Because the <code>TARGET_DATASOURCE</code> engine is a MergeTree, you can use fields that you expect to be updated as sorting keys in the ReplacingMergeTree.</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-header"><div class="snippet-headerInfo overflow"><h5 class="snippet-title as-font--caption-bold as-cap overflow mr-4" title="post_snapshot.datasource">post_snapshot.datasource</h5></div></div><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">SCHEMA &gt;
    `post_id` Int32,
    `views` Int32,
    `likes` Int32,
    `tag` String,
    `ts` DateTime,
    `snapshot_ts` DateTime

ENGINE &quot;MergeTree&quot;
ENGINE_PARTITION_KEY &quot;&quot;
ENGINE_SORTING_KEY &quot;tag, post_id&quot;
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><h2 id="hybrid-approach-using-lambda-architecture" class="t-h4 font-semibold mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="12.0">Hybrid approach using Lambda architecture<a class="headerlink" href="#hybrid-approach-using-lambda-architecture" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h2><p>Snapshots might decrease data freshness, and running Copy Pipes too frequently might be more expensive than materializations. A way to mitigate these issues is to combine batch and real-time processing, reading the latest snapshot and incorporating the changes that happened since then.</p><p>This pattern is described in the <a href="/docs/forward/work-with-data/optimize/guides/lambda-architecture">Lambda architecture</a> guide.</p><p>Using the <code>post_snapshot</code> data source created before, the real-time Pipe would be like the following:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-header"><div class="snippet-headerInfo overflow"><h5 class="snippet-title as-font--caption-bold as-cap overflow mr-4" title="latest_values.pipe">latest_values.pipe</h5></div></div><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">NODE get_latest_changes
SQL &gt;

    SELECT
        max(timestamp) last_ts,
        post_id,
        argMax(views, timestamp) views,
        argMax(likes, timestamp) likes,
        argMax(tag, timestamp) tag
    FROM posts_info_rmt
    WHERE timestamp &gt; (SELECT max(snapshot_ts) FROM post_snapshot)
    GROUP BY post_id

NODE get_snapshot
SQL &gt;

    SELECT
        last_ts,
        post_id,
        views,
        likes,
        tag
    FROM post_snapshot
    WHERE snapshot_ts = (SELECT max(snapshot_ts) FROM post_snapshot)
    AND post_id NOT IN (SELECT post_id FROM get_latest_changes)


NODE combine_both
SQL &gt;

    SELECT * FROM get_snapshot
    UNION ALL
    SELECT * FROM get_latest_changes

</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><h2 id="a-note-on-using-argmax-with-null-values" class="t-h4 font-semibold mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="12.0">A note on using argMax with null values<a class="headerlink" href="#a-note-on-using-argmax-with-null-values" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h2><p>Here are the definitions for <code>argMax</code> functions:</p><ul><li><code>argMaxState</code>: used to pipe a constantly updating max state into a materialized view.</li><li><code>argMaxMerge</code>: used to query a max state value out of a materialized view.</li></ul><p><strong>When dealing with null values, <code>argMax</code> functions might not behave as you expect.</strong> In raw queries, you might see a null value for the most recent record. However, when data is piped into an AggregatingMergeTree materialized view using <code>argMaxState</code> and later queried using <code>argMaxMerge</code>, the result can be different.</p><p>Returning to the social media analytics example, imagine you want to track most recent time when a post was flagged.</p><p>The raw query would be as follows:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-header"><div class="snippet-headerInfo overflow"><h5 class="snippet-title as-font--caption-bold as-cap overflow mr-4" title="get_latest_flagged_at_raw.pipe">get_latest_flagged_at_raw.pipe</h5></div></div><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default"># This returns `null` if the most recent record&#x27;s `flaggedAt` value is null.

NODE get_latest_flagged_at_raw
SQL &gt;

    SELECT flaggedAt
    FROM posts
    WHERE post_id = &#x27;abc123&#x27;
    ORDER BY timestamp DESC
    LIMIT 1
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><p>First, data is aggregated into a materialized view with a pipe that uses <code>argMaxState</code>:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-header"><div class="snippet-headerInfo overflow"><h5 class="snippet-title as-font--caption-bold as-cap overflow mr-4" title="get_latest_flagged_at_mat.pipe">get_latest_flagged_at_mat.pipe</h5></div></div><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">NODE get_latest_flagged_at
SQL &gt;

    SELECT argMaxState(flaggedAt, timestamp)
    FROM posts

TYPE materialized
DATASOURCE post_analytics_mv
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><p>Later, the aggregated state is merged with <code>argMaxMerge</code> when the materialized view is queried:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-header"><div class="snippet-headerInfo overflow"><h5 class="snippet-title as-font--caption-bold as-cap overflow mr-4" title="get_latest_flagged_at_mat.pipe">get_latest_flagged_at_mat.pipe</h5></div></div><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">NODE get_absolute_latest_flagged_at
SQL &gt;

    SELECT argMaxMerge(flaggedAt)
    FROM post_analytics_mv
    WHERE post_id = &#x27;abc123&#x27;
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><p>Although you might expect a <code>null</code> result because the raw query returned <code>null</code>, the merging process prefers any non‑null value over a null value—even if its associated timestamp is lower. The result is the most recent non‑null <code>flaggedAt</code> value.</p><h4 id="why-this-happens-and-workaround" class="t-body-2 font-medium mt-8 mb-2">Why this happens and workaround<a class="headerlink" href="#why-this-happens-and-workaround" title="Permalink to this heading" data-pagefind-ignore="true">¶</a></h4><p>During the merge process, the materialized view combines key‑value candidate states. A key-value candidate in this example would be <code>timestamp</code> and <code>flaggedAt</code>. If one candidate has a non‑null <code>flaggedAt</code> and another has a null value for <code>flaggedAt</code>, the non‑null value &quot;wins&quot; regardless of its timestamp. This behavior is inherent to the merging logic in <code>argMaxMerge</code> . It explains why in an argMaxMerge query, you might not get the absolute max.</p><p>To prevent the merging behavior from overriding a null with a non‑null candidate, you need to handle null values explicitly before they enter the materialized view. One common approach is to transform null values to a known default—often the Unix epoch <code>1970-01-01 00:00:00</code>. However, be aware that such conversions produce &quot;fake&quot; values which must be recognized in subsequent processing.</p><p>Assume your raw data includes a flaggedAt column, which may contain nulls. You can pre-process the data during aggregation as follows:</p><div class="max-w-full overflow-auto mb-4"><div class="snippet"><div class="snippet-header"><div class="snippet-headerInfo overflow"><h5 class="snippet-title as-font--caption-bold as-cap overflow mr-4" title="get_latest_flagged_at_no_nulls.pipe">get_latest_flagged_at_no_nulls.pipe</h5></div></div><div class="snippet-code-container"><div class="snippet-code is-visible"><pre class="cm-s-default">NODE get_latest_flagged_at_no_nulls
SQL &gt;

    SELECT
        argMaxState(
            CASE
                WHEN flaggedAt IS NULL
                THEN toDateTime(&#x27;1970-01-01 00:00:00&#x27;)
                ELSE flaggedAt
            END,
            timestamp
        )
    FROM posts
</pre></div></div><div class="absolute top-0 right-0 p-2"><button class="snippet-copyButton"><svg class="" width="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><g opacity="1"><mask id="w-mask" fill="white"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M13 3H7V9H13V3ZM7 2C6.44772 2 6 2.44772 6 3V9C6 9.55228 6.44772 10 7 10H13C13.5523 10 14 9.55228 14 9V3C14 2.44772 13.5523 2 13 2H7Z"></path></mask><path mask="url(#w-mask)" fill="#1FCC83" d="M7 3V2H6V3H7ZM13 3H14V2H13V3ZM7 9H6V10H7V9ZM13 9V10H14V9H13ZM7 4H13V2H7V4ZM8 9V3H6V9H8ZM13 8H7V10H13V8ZM12 3V9H14V3H12ZM7 3V1C5.89543 1 5 1.89543 5 3H7ZM7 9V3H5V9H7ZM7 9H5C5 10.1046 5.89543 11 7 11V9ZM13 9H7V11H13V9ZM13 9V11C14.1046 11 15 10.1046 15 9H13ZM13 3V9H15V3H13ZM13 3H15C15 1.89543 14.1046 1 13 1V3ZM7 3H13V1H7V3Z"></path><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M6 7H3V13H9V10H10V13C10 13.5523 9.55228 14 9 14H3C2.44772 14 2 13.5523 2 13V7C2 6.44772 2.44772 6 3 6H6V7Z" fill="#1FCC83"></path></g></svg></button></div></div></div><p>Here, a CASE expression is used to convert any null flaggedAt values into the default datetime 1970-01-01 00:00:00.<!-- --> <!-- -->This ensures that during the merge, the aggregation logic processes these explicit default values rather than implicitly &quot;overriding&quot; nulls.</p><div class="my-4 flex items-start gap-2 py-3 px-4 rounded border border-v-border bg-v-callout-caution text-[#856100]"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" fill="none" viewBox="0 0 16 16" class="inline shrink-0 mt-px h-5"><path fill="currentColor" d="M8.333 10.216a.666.666 0 1 0 0 1.332.666.666 0 0 0 0-1.332m7.114.98L10.08 1.862a2 2 0 0 0-3.493 0l-5.334 9.334a2 2 0 0 0 1.707 3.02h10.747a2 2 0 0 0 1.74-3.02m-1.154 1.333a.67.67 0 0 1-.586.34H2.96a.67.67 0 0 1-.587-.34.67.67 0 0 1 0-.667L7.707 2.53a.667.667 0 0 1 1.186 0l5.367 9.333a.67.67 0 0 1 .033.68zm-5.96-7.647a.667.667 0 0 0-.666.667v2.667a.667.667 0 1 0 1.333 0V5.549a.667.667 0 0 0-.667-.667"></path></svg><div class="text-v-text"><p>Since <code>1970-01-01 00:00:00</code> is used as a default placeholder, ensure that any downstream logic differentiates between genuine datetime values and these default values.</p></div></div><h2 id="next-steps" class="t-h4 font-semibold mt-10 mb-2" data-pagefind-weight="12.0">Next steps<a efault\"]\n3c:I[57187,[\"5878\",\"static/chunks/9da6db1e-fe3f3691e817470b.js\",\"314\",\"static/chunks/32ea55aa-334b9848c750da09.js\",\"4960\",\"static/chunks/8b30ef62-8e1a3557163ef34d.js\",\"9729\",\"static/chunks/72b2f85d-e46ed6c2f9c8d9d7.js\",\"5501\",\"static/chunks/c16f53c3-0400c7825a916970.js\",\"8370\",\"static/chunks/8370-7a9554878d1b9d35.js\",\"7648\",\"static/chunks/7648-2c0c3a3dc3702719.js\",\"2694\",\"static/chunks/2694-6ee008eb8be89699.js\",\"9267\",\"static/chunks/9267-89ff5dc708370f39.js\",\"1284\",\"static/chunks/1284-f30446673b9ba073.js\",\"7867\",\"static/chunks/7867-6d0484accd87a171.js\",\"3145\",\"static/chunks/3145-ca0c40eb1bb881d8.js\",\"5107\",\"static/chunks/5107-ef688f2fbbe55825.js\",\"2418\",\"static/chunks/2418-b0d27e6f47546ed6.js\",\"4144\",\"static/chunks/4144-34f98e6e70550e12.js\",\"1147\",\"static/chunks/1147-ac53c80b8f8a3921.js\",\"1749\",\"static/chunks/1749-b2df567f1b8974df.js\",\"5643\",\"static/chunks/5643-5ba78075e5c8bae2.js\",\"1796\",\"static/chunks/1796-b956fe6fe21dbf17.js\",\"787\",\"static/chunks/787-09fc1907ef45c351.js\",\"996\",\"static/chunks/996-ce0ceee74ea8f43a.js\",\"7432\",\"static/chunks/7432-03643de0998568d4.js\",\"1384\",\"static/chunks/app/(forward)/forward/%5B%5B...slug%5D%5D/page-8347ce85311902e7.js\"],\"default\"]\n21:T34ae,"])</script><script>self.__next_f.push([1,"---\ntitle: Deduplicate data in your data source\ntags: realtime-cdc\nmeta:\ndescription: Learn several strategies for deduplicating data in Tinybird.\n---\n\n# Deduplicate data in your data source\n\nSometimes you might need to deduplicate data, for example to receive updates or data from a transactional database through CDC. You might want to retrieve only the latest data point, or keep a historic record of the evolution of the attributes of an object over time.\nBecause Tinybird doesn't enforce uniqueness for primary keys when inserting rows, you need to follow different strategies to deduplicate data with minimal side effects.\n\n## Deduplication strategies\n\nYou can use one of the following strategies to deduplicate your data.\n\n{% table %}\n  * Method\n  * When to use  \n  ---\n  * [Deduplicate at query time](#deduplicate-at-query-time)\n  * Deduplicate data at query time if you are still prototyping or the data source is small.\n  ---\n  * [Use ReplacingMergeTree](#use-the-replacingmergetree-engine)\n  * Use `ReplacingMergeTree` or `AggregatingMergeTree` for greater performance.\n  ---\n  * [Snapshot based deduplication](#snapshot-based-deduplication)\n  * If data freshness isn't required, generate periodic snapshots of the data and take advantage of subsequent materialized views for rollups.\n  ---\n  * [Hybrid approach using Lambda architecture](#hybrid-approach-using-lambda-architecture)\n  * When you need to overcome engine approach limitations while preserving freshness, combine approaches in a Lambda architecture.\n  ---\n  * Using argMax with null values\n  * \n{% /table %}\n\n{% callout type=\"tip\" %}\nFor dimensional and small tables, a periodical full replace is usually the best option.\n{% /callout %}\n\n## Example case\n\nConsider a dataset from a social media analytics company that wants to track some data content over time. You receive an event with the latest info for each post, identified by `post_id`. The three fields, `views`, `likes`, `tags`, vary from event to event. For example:\n\n```ndjson {% title=\"post.ndjson\" %}\n{ \"timestamp\": \"2024-07-02T02:22:17\", \"post_id\": 956, \"views\": 856875, \"likes\": 2321, \"tags\": \"Sports\" }\n```\n\n## Deduplicate at query time\n\nImagine you're only interested in the latest value of views for each post. In that case, you can deduplicate data on `post_id` and get the latest value with these strategies:\n\n- Get the max date for each post in a subquery and then filter by its results.\n\n- Group data by `post_id` and use the `argMax` function.\n\n- Use the `LIMIT BY` clause.\n\nSelect `Subquery`, `argMax`, or `LIMIT BY` to see the example queries for each.\n\n{% tabs initial=\"Subquery\" %}\n{% tab label=\"Subquery\"  %}\n\n```sql {% title=\"Deduplicating data on post_id using Subquery\" %}\nSELECT *\nFROM posts_info\nWHERE (post_id, timestamp) IN\n(\n    SELECT\n        post_id,\n        max(timestamp)\n    FROM posts_info\n    GROUP BY post_id\n)\n```\n\n{% /tab %}\n{% tab label=\"argMax\" %}\n\n```sql {% title=\"Deduplicating data on post_id using argMax\" %}\nSELECT\n    max(timestamp) last_ts,\n    post_id,\n    argMax(views, timestamp) views,\n    argMax(likes, timestamp) likes,\n    argMax(tag, timestamp) tag\nFROM posts_info\nGROUP BY post_id\nORDER BY last_ts, post_id\n```\n\n{% /tab %}\n{% tab label=\"LIMIT BY\" %}\n\n```sql {% title=\"Deduplicating data on post_id using LIMIT BY\" %}\nSELECT *\nFROM posts_info\nORDER BY post_id, timestamp DESC\nLIMIT 1 BY post_id\n```\n\n{% /tab %}\n\n{% /tabs %}\n\nDepending on your data and how you define the sorting keys in your data sources to store it on disk, one approach is faster than the others.\n\nIn general, deduplicating at query time is fine if the size of your data is small. If you have lots of data, use a specific Engine that takes care of deduplication for you.\n\n## Use the ReplacingMergeTree engine\n\nIf you've lots of data and you're interested in the latest insertion for each unique key, use the [ReplacingMergeTree](/sql-reference/engines/replacingmergetree) engine with the following options: `ENGINE_SORTING_KEY`, `ENGINE_VER`, and `ENGINE_IS_DELETED`.\n\n- Rows with the same `ENGINE_SORTING_KEY` are deduplicated. You can select one or more columns.\n  \n- If you specify a type for `ENGINE_VER`, the row with the highest `ENGINE_VER` for each unique `ENGINE_SORTING_KEY` is kept, for example a timestamp.\n\n- `ENGINE_IS_DELETED` is only active if you use `ENGINE_VER`. This column determines whether the row represents the state or is to be deleted; `1` is a deleted row, `0` is a state row. The type must be `UInt8`.\n\n- You can omit `ENGINE_VER`, so that the last inserted row for each unique `ENGINE_SORTING_KEY` is kept.\n\n{% callout type=\"caution\" %}\nDo not build materialized views with an AggregatingMergeTree on top of a ReplacingMergeTree. The target data source will always contain duplicates due to the incremental nature of materialized views.\n{% /callout %}\n\n### Define a data source\n\nDefine a data source like the following:\n\n```tb {% title=\"post_views_rmt.datasource\" %}\nDESCRIPTION \u003e\n    data source to save post info. ReplacingMergeTree Engine.\n\nSCHEMA \u003e\n    `post_id` Int32 `json:$.post_id`,\n    `views` Int32 `json:$.views`,\n    `likes` Int32 `json:$.likes`,\n    `tag` String `json:$.tag`,\n    `timestamp` DateTime `json:$.timestamp`,\n    `_is_deleted` UInt8 `json:$._is_deleted`\n\nENGINE \"ReplacingMergeTree\"\nENGINE_PARTITION_KEY \"\"\nENGINE_SORTING_KEY \"post_id\"\nENGINE_VER \"timestamp\"\nENGINE_IS_DELETED \"_is_deleted\"\n```\n\nReplacingMergeTree deduplicates during a merge, and merges can't be controlled. Consider adding the `FINAL` clause, or an alternative deduplication method, to apply the merge at query time. Note also that rows are masked, not removed, when using `FINAL`.\n\n{% tabs initial=\"FINAL\" %}\n\n{% tab label=\"FINAL\"  %}\n\n```sql {% title=\"Deduplicating data on post_id using FINAL\" %}\nSELECT *\nFROM posts_info_rmt FINAL\n```\n\n{% /tab %}\n\n{% tab label=\"Subquery\"  %}\n\n```sql {% title=\"Deduplicating data on post_id using Subquery\" %}\nSELECT *\nFROM posts_info_rmt\nWHERE (post_id, timestamp) IN\n(\n    SELECT\n        post_id,\n        max(timestamp)\n    FROM posts_info_rmt\n    GROUP BY post_id\n)\n```\n\n{% /tab %}\n\n{% tab label=\"argMax\" %}\n\n```sql {% title=\"Deduplicating data on post_id using argMax\" %}\nSELECT\n    max(timestamp) last_ts,\n    post_id,\n    argMax(views, timestamp) views,\n    argMax(likes, timestamp) likes,\n    argMax(tag, timestamp) tag\nFROM posts_info_rmt\nGROUP BY post_id\nORDER BY last_ts, post_id\n```\n\n{% /tab %}\n\n{% tab label=\"LIMIT BY\" %}\n\n```sql {% title=\"Deduplicating data on post_id using LIMIT BY\" %}\nSELECT *\nFROM posts_info_rmt\nORDER BY post_id, timestamp DESC\nLIMIT 1 BY post_id\n```\n\n{% /tab %}\n\n{% /tabs %}\n\nYou can define the `posts_info_rmt` as the landing data source, the one you send events to, or as a materialized view from `posts_info`. You can also create a data source with an `AggregatingMergeTree` Engine using `maxState(ts)` and `argMaxState(field,ts)`.\n\n## Snapshot based deduplication\n\nUse [Copy Pipes](/forward/work-with-data/optimize/copy-pipes) to take a query result and write it to a new data source in the following situations:\n\n- You need other Sorting Keys that might change with updates.\n- You need to do rollups and want to use materialized views.\n- Response times are too long with a `ReplacingMergeTree`.\n\nThe following is an example snapshot:\n\n```tb {% title=\"post_generate_snapshot.pipe\" %}\nNODE gen_snapshot\nSQL \u003e\n\n    SELECT\n        post_id,\n        argMax(views, timestamp) views,\n        argMax(likes, timestamp) likes,\n        argMax(tag, timestamp) tag,\n        max(timestamp) as ts,\n        toStartOfMinute(now()) - INTERVAL 1 MINUTE as snapshot_ts\n    FROM posts_info\n    WHERE timestamp \u003c= toStartOfMinute(now()) - INTERVAL 1 MINUTE\n    GROUP BY post_id\n\nTYPE COPY\nTARGET_DATASOURCE post_snapshot\nCOPY_MODE replace\nCOPY_SCHEDULE 0 * * * *\n```\n\nBecause the `TARGET_DATASOURCE` engine is a MergeTree, you can use fields that you expect to be updated as sorting keys in the ReplacingMergeTree.\n\n```tb {% title=\"post_snapshot.datasource\" %}\nSCHEMA \u003e\n    `post_id` Int32,\n    `views` Int32,\n    `likes` Int32,\n    `tag` String,\n    `ts` DateTime,\n    `snapshot_ts` DateTime\n\nENGINE \"MergeTree\"\nENGINE_PARTITION_KEY \"\"\nENGINE_SORTING_KEY \"tag, post_id\"\n```\n\n## Hybrid approach using Lambda architecture\n\nSnapshots might decrease data freshness, and running Copy Pipes too frequently might be more expensive than materializations. A way to mitigate these issues is to combine batch and real-time processing, reading the latest snapshot and incorporating the changes that happened since then.\n\nThis pattern is described in the [Lambda architecture](/forward/work-with-data/optimize/guides/lambda-architecture) guide.\n\nUsing the `post_snapshot` data source created before, the real-time Pipe would be like the following:\n\n```tb {% title=\"latest_values.pipe\" %}\nNODE get_latest_changes\nSQL \u003e\n\n    SELECT\n        max(timestamp) last_ts,\n        post_id,\n        argMax(views, timestamp) views,\n        argMax(likes, timestamp) likes,\n        argMax(tag, timestamp) tag\n    FROM posts_info_rmt\n    WHERE timestamp \u003e (SELECT max(snapshot_ts) FROM post_snapshot)\n    GROUP BY post_id\n\nNODE get_snapshot\nSQL \u003e\n\n    SELECT\n        last_ts,\n        post_id,\n        views,\n        likes,\n        tag\n    FROM post_snapshot\n    WHERE snapshot_ts = (SELECT max(snapshot_ts) FROM post_snapshot)\n    AND post_id NOT IN (SELECT post_id FROM get_latest_changes)\n\n\nNODE combine_both\nSQL \u003e\n\n    SELECT * FROM get_snapshot\n    UNION ALL\n    SELECT * FROM get_latest_changes\n\n```\n\n## A note on using argMax with null values\n\nHere are the definitions for `argMax` functions:\n\n* `argMaxState`: used to pipe a constantly updating max state into a materialized view.\n* `argMaxMerge`: used to query a max state value out of a materialized view.\n\n__When dealing with null values, `argMax` functions might not behave as you expect.__ In raw queries, you might see a null value for the most recent record. However, when data is piped into an AggregatingMergeTree materialized view using `argMaxState` and later queried using `argMaxMerge`, the result can be different.\n\nReturning to the social media analytics example, imagine you want to track most recent time when a post was flagged.\n\nThe raw query would be as follows:\n\n```tb {% title=\"get_latest_flagged_at_raw.pipe\" %}\n# This returns `null` if the most recent record's `flaggedAt` value is null.\n\nNODE get_latest_flagged_at_raw\nSQL \u003e\n\n    SELECT flaggedAt\n    FROM posts\n    WHERE post_id = 'abc123'\n    ORDER BY timestamp DESC\n    LIMIT 1\n```\n\nFirst, data is aggregated into a materialized view with a pipe that uses `argMaxState`:\n\n```tb {% title=\"get_latest_flagged_at_mat.pipe\" %}\nNODE get_latest_flagged_at\nSQL \u003e\n\n    SELECT argMaxState(flaggedAt, timestamp)\n    FROM posts\n\nTYPE materialized\nDATASOURCE post_analytics_mv\n```\n\nLater, the aggregated state is merged with `argMaxMerge` when the materialized view is queried:\n\n```tb {% title=\"get_latest_flagged_at_mat.pipe\" %}\nNODE get_absolute_latest_flagged_at\nSQL \u003e\n\n    SELECT argMaxMerge(flaggedAt)\n    FROM post_analytics_mv\n    WHERE post_id = 'abc123'\n```\n\nAlthough you might expect a `null` result because the raw query returned `null`, the merging process prefers any non‑null value over a null value—even if its associated timestamp is lower. The result is the most recent non‑null `flaggedAt` value.\n\n#### Why this happens and workaround\n\nDuring the merge process, the materialized view combines key‑value candidate states. A key-value candidate in this example would be `timestamp` and `flaggedAt`. If one candidate has a non‑null `flaggedAt` and another has a null value for `flaggedAt`, the non‑null value \"wins\" regardless of its timestamp. This behavior is inherent to the merging logic in `argMaxMerge` . It explains why in an argMaxMerge query, you might not get the absolute max.\n\nTo prevent the merging behavior from overriding a null with a non‑null candidate, you need to handle null values explicitly before they enter the materialized view. One common approach is to transform null values to a known default—often the Unix epoch `1970-01-01 00:00:00`. However, be aware that such conversions produce \"fake\" values which must be recognized in subsequent processing.\n\nAssume your raw data includes a flaggedAt column, which may contain nulls. You can pre-process the data during aggregation as follows:\n\n```tb {% title=\"get_latest_flagged_at_no_nulls.pipe\" %}\nNODE get_latest_flagged_at_no_nulls\nSQL \u003e\n\n    SELECT\n        argMaxState(\n            CASE\n                WHEN flaggedAt IS NULL\n                THEN toDateTime('1970-01-01 00:00:00')\n                ELSE flaggedAt\n            END,\n            timestamp\n        )\n    FROM posts\n```\n\nHere, a CASE expression is used to convert any null flaggedAt values into the default datetime 1970-01-01 00:00:00.\nThis ensures that during the merge, the aggregation logic processes these explicit default values rather than implicitly \"overriding\" nulls.\n\n{% callout type=\"caution\" %}\nSince `1970-01-01 00:00:00` is used as a default placeholder, ensure that any downstream logic differentiates between genuine datetime values and these default values.\n{% /callout %}\n\n## Next steps\n\n- Read the [materialized views docs](/forward/work-with-data/optimize/materialized-views).\n- Read the [Lambda architecture guide](/forward/work-with-data/optimize/guides/lambda-architecture).\n- Publish your data with [API endpoints](/forward/work-with-data/publish-data/endpoints)."])</script><script>self.__next_f.push([1,"37:{\"fill\":\"currentColor\",\"d\":\"M8.333 10.216a.666.666 0 1 0 0 1.332.666.666 0 0 0 2.53a.667.667 0 0 1 1.186 0l5.367 9.333a.67.67 0 0 1 .033.68zm-5.96-7.647a.667.667 0 0 0-.666.667v2.667a.667.667 0 1 0 1.333 0V5.549a.667.667 0 0
